  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_42874a55-b493-4ec7-9346-1540370dbb1a'

<span id="freeTextContainer9344049774133993390">She was just a little girl, with a tiny horn in the center of her forehead, funny-looking feet, beautiful silver hair, and several curious powers: the ability to purify air and water, make plants grow, and heal scars and broken bones. A trio of grizzled prospectors found her drifting in an escape pod amid the asteroids, adopted her, and took her to the bandit planet Kezdet</span>
  <span id="freeText9344049774133993390" style="display:none">She was just a little girl, with a tiny horn in the center of her forehead, funny-looking feet, beautiful silver hair, and several curious powers: the ability to purify air and water, make plants grow, and heal scars and broken bones. A trio of grizzled prospectors found her drifting in an escape pod amid the asteroids, adopted her, and took her to the bandit planet Kezdet, a place where no questions are asked and the girl might grow up free.<br /><br />But Kezdet has its own dark secret. The prosperity of the planet is based on a hideous trade in child slave labor, administered by "The Piper" -- a mystery man with special plans for Acorna and her powers. But free little girls have a way of growing into freedom-loving young women, and Acorna has special plans all her own. . .</span>

<div id="review_975493180" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/975493180" />
    <a title="Jerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5855981-jerry"><img alt="Jerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520438201p2/5855981.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/975493180?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jerry" href="/user/show/5855981-jerry">Jerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061057892" href="/book/show/829805.Acorna">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5855981-jerry?shelf=a-to-z-challenge-2017">a-to-z-challenge-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer975493180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3827506841797837577">All the way back in 2001, a short story called "The Smallest Dragonboy" in my seventh grade literature textbook served as my introduction to the great, now late author Anne McCaffrey. After finishing that story, we watched an interview with Ms. McCaffrey--was it on laserdisc or DVD? I'm still not sure!--where she talked about how, despite some of her stories having female leads, she didn't have any Cinderella-style characters "because Cinderella was a wimp!"<br/><br/>At the time I read/listened to that st</span>
  <span id="freeText3827506841797837577" style="display:none">All the way back in 2001, a short story called "The Smallest Dragonboy" in my seventh grade literature textbook served as my introduction to the great, now late author Anne McCaffrey. After finishing that story, we watched an interview with Ms. McCaffrey--was it on laserdisc or DVD? I'm still not sure!--where she talked about how, despite some of her stories having female leads, she didn't have any Cinderella-style characters "because Cinderella was a wimp!"<br /><br />At the time I read/listened to that story in class, I wasn't much of a reader; I was all about Pokémon, Game Boy Color, <i>Hoyle Board Games</i>, and the music of dc Talk, all of which I could engage in while hardly even cracking open any literature (at least, none worth reading). It wasn't until my junior year of high school was almost over that I rediscovered the love for reading I had when I was in elementary school, all thanks to a <i>Star Wars</i> Expanded Universe novel I bought at a garage sale. Still, I remembered that short story and video interview from seventh grade; years later, I came across the <i>Acorna</i> series at a garage sale, and that was my first experience with the works of Anne McCaffrey in a long time.<br /><br />Reading it now--for the sixth time!--I had forgotten some of the details of the plot; then again, as many books as I read in just a year's time, there's no way I could remember them all. Anne McCaffrey and Margaret Ball work great together, and spin a fun sci-fi/fantasy yarn with a likable heroine and plenty of plot twists. The only downside is that some potentially offensive content--d-words and h-words, sexual references, talk of prostitution, etc.--found its way into the mix, which could keep some discerning readers from enjoying this. If that kind of thing bothers you, proceed with caution.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3827506841797837577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061057892" href="/book/show/829805.Acorna">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1867254608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10641162334384274207">Magical and dazzling, this peculiar fantasy novel about a girl who is part unicorn is one of the most interesting books I've read so far this year. Although at times I thought it was veering off the path of imaginative and becoming more typical, I still really enjoyed it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_26106838" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26106838" />
    <a title="r." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1283231-r"><img alt="r." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376350955p2/1283231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26106838?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="r." class="user" itemprop="url" name="r." href="/user/show/1283231-r">r.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283231-r?shelf=publication-contemporary">publication-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283231-r?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26106838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16035368384091296518">I read this as part of a big cleaning out of the many books I've purchased since my teen years, but never actually read. I expected it to be an earnest story about a unicorn girl (named Acorna nonetheless) and as such possibly humorously bad. One mark in its favor is that there was a very definite wry tone to the narrative, so most silliness seems intentional. But that's pretty much the only mark in its favor.<br/><br/>Sadly, this book is just...bad. It's badly written and badly structured, with constant </span>
  <span id="freeText16035368384091296518" style="display:none">I read this as part of a big cleaning out of the many books I've purchased since my teen years, but never actually read. I expected it to be an earnest story about a unicorn girl (named Acorna nonetheless) and as such possibly humorously bad. One mark in its favor is that there was a very definite wry tone to the narrative, so most silliness seems intentional. But that's pretty much the only mark in its favor.<br /><br />Sadly, this book is just...bad. It's badly written and badly structured, with constant POV changes, often from one paragraph to the next, a plodding pace, and a complete lack of rising action or climax.<br /><br />It's as if the authors forgot that in a book things not only need to happen, but need to happen in a way that's interesting and engaging. Instead, the characters (all quite shallow) just sort of wander about and do stuff with little to no competent resistance or drama. There's never any suspense or sense of danger despite the fact that the characters are ostensibly attempting very dangerous things. Every antagonist either turns out to mean them no harm and becomes a massively powerful ally or is instantly and easily dispatched by aforementioned massively powerful allies. So, instead of anything remotely entertaining you're basically just reading a dull account of how some dudes easily accomplished a thing.<br /><br />This is the part where I would usually complain about the relationships, but there's not much to complain about. There are a couple of people who appear to vaguely like each other and in the end maybe move in together or get married or something with no actual development leading into this. There are a couple of other people who like each other in an even more vague manner than the previous couple, one of whom suddenly confronts the other about it 3/4 of the way through the book. They proceed to have a brief conversation in which no conclusions are reached and absolutely nothing is resolved, and then it's completely forgotten about for the rest of the book. I suppose it would be disappointing if you had any reason to care about any of these people? I don't know.<br /><br />At any rate, I expected this book to be bad, but it was surprising in the way that it was bad. Instead of earnest, melodramatic cheese bad, it was shoddily-thrown-together, barely-a-story bad.<br /><br />0/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="16035368384091296518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_33477781" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33477781" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1555261-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1224441973p2/1555261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33477781?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1555261-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1555261-megan?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33477781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4420822241366574527">Okay, this is going to be of a review for the entire series of Acorna books because, well, there are alot of them and I would get carpal tunnel if I wrote an individual review of each book.<br/><br/>Basically this is the story of 2 asteroid miners who come across a strange space pod that has a little girl that resembles a unicorn inside of it. As she is only a baby and there is no one to care for her, they quickly adopt her. This creates all sorts of problems as she is highly sought after as proof of alie</span>
  <span id="freeText4420822241366574527" style="display:none">Okay, this is going to be of a review for the entire series of Acorna books because, well, there are alot of them and I would get carpal tunnel if I wrote an individual review of each book.<br /><br />Basically this is the story of 2 asteroid miners who come across a strange space pod that has a little girl that resembles a unicorn inside of it. As she is only a baby and there is no one to care for her, they quickly adopt her. This creates all sorts of problems as she is highly sought after as proof of alien life. So the three miners head to the planet Kezdet, where they have heard that with enough money, one can live without being bothered.<br /><br />However Kezdet has its own problems, namely that its entire economy relies on children working as literal slaves. The 3 miners, along with Acorna, work to end this terrible tragedy.<br /><br />In later books, the story of searching for acorna's people takes place, along with her finding a boyfriend who is physically and emotionally scarred, and finding out that her people are at war with a bug-like race, the Khleevi who are responsible for not only her being an orphan but also for her boyfriends scars as well.<br /><br />Up until this point the story is pretty straightforward and easy to understand and really quite enjoyable. Anne McCaffrey once again is able to create a world that is easily understandable, with characters you can identify with.<br /><br />However, eventually as the series wore on, i think she ran out of plot developments and the story just turns downright well, bizarre. Acorna's boyfriend finds a way to travel back in time and he tries to change history so that he is never captured by the khleevi and tortured (can't really blame the guy but still) meanwhile while doing this he somehow traps acorna in a time loop so that she isn't in the past with him or in the present with everyone else but somewhere else altogether. At this point the story got so incredibly technical, hard to follow and really just unbelievable that I stopped reading before finding out how they fixed it. But I assume they did, becasue there is apparently another series entirely that follows thier children and it is somewhat difficult to have kids if you are stuck in some sort of time vortex</span>
  <a data-text-id="4420822241366574527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10699352627137036622" style="display:none">I found this book in my school library when I started grade 9, and I thought it sounded like the absolute most ridiculous book in the history of the world! I spent the next three years making fun of it, and my friends and I even had a sort of inside joke about it. I mean, come on! This is a story about an orphaned girl who has a unicorn horn sticking out of her forehead! Puh-lease! In grade 11, I finally read it, sort of as a joke, and it turned out to actually be pretty good, when it comes to science fiction. If you overlook the fact that the main character has a horn in her head, it's a pretty good story line!</span>

<div id="review_943537563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/943537563" />
    <a title="Dianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1401819-dianne"><img alt="Dianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604666390p2/1401819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/943537563?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dianne" href="/user/show/1401819-dianne">Dianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6567144-the-unicorn-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer943537563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16348552967618716456">I had heard of the late author Anne McCaffrey but had never felt curious enough to read her young adult series. Then I came upon Acorna, decided, what the heck, and picked it up. I am so very glad I did.<br/><br/>This book grabbed me and sucked me in right from the get-go. The characters are ‘real’ if you know what I mean…well as real as a girl with a silver horn (unicorn) can be!<br/>This story, at least the first half-reminds me very much of another of my favorite authors Anne Bishop and the book “Written in</span>
  <span id="freeText16348552967618716456" style="display:none">I had heard of the late author Anne McCaffrey but had never felt curious enough to read her young adult series. Then I came upon Acorna, decided, what the heck, and picked it up. I am so very glad I did.<br /><br />This book grabbed me and sucked me in right from the get-go. The characters are ‘real’ if you know what I mean…well as real as a girl with a silver horn (unicorn) can be!<br />This story, at least the first half-reminds me very much of another of my favorite authors Anne Bishop and the book “Written in Red” a sort of paranormal fish-out-of-water type of book. This novel also has some elements of Ms Bishops “Black Jewels” trilogy, but is much less sexual.<br /><br />That is somewhat how Acorna starts – with a foundling with a horn, adopted by three metal prospectors who hunt for ore on asteroids and such. Acorna definitely has a lot to learn about how to be human…or does she really?<br /><br />There is a lot of excitement, tragedy and humor. There is fantastic world building and character growth in this first installment.There is not a huge amount of scientific info dumps and very little about the science of space travel –it is a world that needs no explanation, it just is. And I loved it.<br /><br />There is some romance, but mostly implied. I hope this will be developed in future books.<br /><br />If the rest of the series stands up to this novel then I will be a happy camper. I will very much mourn the passing of such an author as Ms. McCaffrey but be content that at least I DID find her, and look forward to reading all of her books that I have missed until now.<br />This is said to be an adult series, but I can see no reason that teens wouldn’t like it also. As far as I can remember there is no horrible language and the scary parts are something most teens can handle easily.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16348552967618716456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/771849453" />
    <a title="Lady ♥ Belleza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7773122-lady-belleza"><img alt="Lady ♥ Belleza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520522061p2/7773122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer13635686004804300222">Recently I watched a review for “The Last Unicorn”, it was based on a book, however when I went looking for the book I couldn’t find it. I found this book however. Having read all of the “Dragonriders of Pern” series by Anne McCaffrey I decided to give this series a try.<br/><br/>This was an enjoyable book.   <span id="freeText13635686004804300222" style="display:none">Recently I watched a review for “The Last Unicorn”, it was based on a book, however when I went looking for the book I couldn’t find it. I found this book however. Having read all of the “Dragonriders of Pern” series by Anne McCaffrey I decided to give this series a try.<br /><br />This was an enjoyable book. It seemed to lack somewhat in characterization and plot. My memories of Dragonriders are a little fuzzy as it was several years ago I read them, but it seems they were much better written. These books boil down to good vs evil. The good being Acorna and her friends, the evil practically everyone else. I say practically everyone because not everyone is evil, but it seems that everyone who is not a friend of Acorna, if they are not evil, they end up becoming her friends.<br /><br />The story starts with 3 space miners finding a floating escape pod and inside it is a little girl, human-like, but not human. Before they can back to their planet they take care of her, they become her ‘uncles’ and as such decide to keep her and raise her as their own. They discover she has some special abilities. Upon returning to their planet they find things have changed, this leads to the first encounter with ‘evil’ and they end up on the run and on a planet Kezdet, which uses child slave labor.<br /><br />What follows is Acorna trying to free the children and acting impulsively, which disrupts the carefully laid plans already in place to save the children.<br /><br />This could almost be considered a young adult book, but there is some violence and adult situations in it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13635686004804300222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_151820547" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151820547" />
    <a title="Iset" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4973578-iset"><img alt="Iset" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563895104p2/4973578.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151820547?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iset" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iset" href="/user/show/4973578-iset">Iset</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552146210" href="/book/show/1017609.Acorna">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4973578-iset?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151820547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4261543009286353668"><br/>This is a re-read of a series I first picked up in my early teens and have re-read a couple of times since. <i>Acorna</i> is the first book in that series. I would describe the series as a sci-fi/fantasy mash-up; it has space travel, futuristic technology, and aliens, but it also has a unicorn girl with magical healing powers who is hailed as various goddesses incarnate and saves enslaved children from evil slavers. Is it any good? Well, let’s just say I enjoyed bits of it more than other parts.<br/><br/>The fir</span>
  <span id="freeText4261543009286353668" style="display:none"><br />This is a re-read of a series I first picked up in my early teens and have re-read a couple of times since. <i>Acorna</i> is the first book in that series. I would describe the series as a sci-fi/fantasy mash-up; it has space travel, futuristic technology, and aliens, but it also has a unicorn girl with magical healing powers who is hailed as various goddesses incarnate and saves enslaved children from evil slavers. Is it any good? Well, let’s just say I enjoyed bits of it more than other parts.<br /><br />The first part of the book I’ve always greatly enjoyed. The comic dynamic of the trio of itinerant miners – Rafik, Gill, and Calum – who discover an alien unicorn girl works really well. The interplay of the three off one another, the comedy of the situation, and there was a real sense of sci-fi here as they travelled the stars undertaking their asteroid mining. Their escape from Amalgamated Mining is always a part I’ve found less thrilling. It all just seems a little too silly and easy to pull off to be believable or gripping. Nevertheless, the quartet goes on their way and now they’re on the run. The escapade with Rafik’s uncle, Hafiz, is another section I’ve always enjoyed. It serves as an interlude from the previous action, the descriptions here are vivid and evocative, and the battle of wits is both an enjoyable read and adds some more comedy into proceedings. The planet-hopping that follows as they struggle to keep afloat and one step ahead of their pursuers is semi-enjoyable, but all the planets they visit are skimmed over too quickly, I felt, with not enough distinguishing description, events, or characters. Finally, the quartet arrives on Kezdet, where Acorna gains a powerful new protector and joins the effort to end child slavery on the planet. It’s here where I felt the book suffers the most. It seemed all too convenient for Acorna to become the ward of her powerful, wealthy, beneficent protector, and all too easy to uncover and bring down the child slavery ring. Many of the characters seemed one-note at this point, even previously established interesting characters such as Calum, Gill, and Rafik, as they each become focused on their individual tasks. Pal Kendoro is just a stereotypical puppy love, his sisters general well-meaning but lacking any really distinctive personality, and the antagonists just seem to be through and through evil without any redeeming features or deeper complexity. It did begin to feel a little bit Mary-Sueish, with Acorna the stunningly beautiful unicorn girl with magical healing powers rescuing the dirty children in rags, who of course immediately love her, from the soulless slavers.<br /><br />One confusing thing as well; the book opens by stating that; “<i>The space/time coordinate system they used has no relationship to Earth, our sun, the Milky Way</i>”, yet throughout characters give distinct Earth backgrounds (e.g. Chinese, British…), use modern idioms and reference historical events (e.g. the abdication of Edward VIII), and even refer to constellations that we know, such as Coma Berenices. Not only was this somewhat confusing, given the initial information that the story is supposed to be set in a fantasy reality/galaxy, but I also found it immensely distracting. As a reader I want to be immersed in this fantasy universe, but every so often the book is reminding me of the real world, not the fictional world I’m supposed to be losing myself in.<br /><br />I’ve liked this series, over the years, but it’s always seemed a little bit simplistic and not quite up to scratch as far as being an amazing read goes. It’s decent, it’s reasonably enjoyable, but no more. I like it, but I don’t love it.<br /><br /><b>6 out of 10</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4261543009286353668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_410377234" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/410377234" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2346680-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357620152p2/2346680.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/410377234?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/2346680-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061798344" href="/book/show/10171579-acorna">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer410377234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6230407478385450518">I first read <u>Acorna: The Unicorn Girl</u> when I was in grade school. This review is for a reread. I remembered the major strokes of this book, but had forgotten the details.<br/><br/>This is the story of three miners and how they find purpose and romance in their lives, catalyzed by the discovery of an extraterrestrial named Acorna. It is the story of the start to the overhaul of an economy in which labor is ill treated - very reminiscent of what happened on Earth in the not too distant past - by a few rich </span>
  <span id="freeText6230407478385450518" style="display:none">I first read <u>Acorna: The Unicorn Girl</u> when I was in grade school. This review is for a reread. I remembered the major strokes of this book, but had forgotten the details.<br /><br />This is the story of three miners and how they find purpose and romance in their lives, catalyzed by the discovery of an extraterrestrial named Acorna. It is the story of the start to the overhaul of an economy in which labor is ill treated - very reminiscent of what happened on Earth in the not too distant past - by a few rich souls who have ethics rather than just morals. It is the story of hope provided to the downtrodden laborers in the person of Acorna. But what it decidedly is not, is the story <i>of</i> the eponymous Acorna.<br /><br />This book deals obliquely with the concepts of extreme poverty, selling children into slavery, pedophilia, and sadomasochism. It also has a scene or two that remind me of Disney's Aladdin when Jasmin escapes the castle and heads out into the market, not understanding that she is going to need money.<br /><br />I cannot speak to the feelings of suspense or not, for as I mention that I have read this novel before, whenever a tricky situation was encountered, I vaguely remembered how it would be resolved and so read on to see that resolution take place. Perhaps you should read a first-read review to see if the tensions are as tense as they are supposed to be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6230407478385450518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Maria Dar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17725536-maria-dar"><img alt="Maria Dar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518827788p2/17725536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2089336681?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Dar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Dar" href="/user/show/17725536-maria-dar">Maria Dar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2089336681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2104800692880127111">Okay, just... no.<br/><br/>I always wanted to read this book as I read a few of Anne McCaffrey's books when I was younger. I enjoyed them, as they had dragons and I absolutely love dragons.<br/><br/>But this... <br/><br/>Despite it having a Unicorn Girl, the thing that really ticked me off was the religion aspect.<br/><br/>Anne McCaffrey skewered up Islam in her novel, presumingly 'updating' the already existing religion with her own preferences, etc. <br/><br/>Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) was the seal of the Prophets. The Quran is perf</span>
  <span id="freeText2104800692880127111" style="display:none">Okay, just... no.<br /><br />I always wanted to read this book as I read a few of Anne McCaffrey's books when I was younger. I enjoyed them, as they had dragons and I absolutely love dragons.<br /><br />But this... <br /><br />Despite it having a Unicorn Girl, the thing that really ticked me off was the religion aspect.<br /><br />Anne McCaffrey skewered up Islam in her novel, presumingly 'updating' the already existing religion with her own preferences, etc. <br /><br />Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) was the seal of the Prophets. The Quran is perfection, never having changed since it's revelation.<br /><br />And yet, Anne McCaffrey decided to bring about more prophets, etc into her story to add to our religion.<br /><br />If you're writing a sci-fi novel, you might as well make up your OWN religion in the stories, not taking one that exists and messing it up. <br /><br />I couldn't finish this novel because of this reason. <br /><br />Otherwise, the premise of the story was initially good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2104800692880127111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Her details were also extremely imaginative without giving so much that I was unable to picture things myself. This is the book that made me an Anna McCaffrey Fan. :D </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/912153431" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/912153431?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/813598-darlene?shelf=mccaffrey">mccaffrey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/813598-darlene?shelf=audible-wishlist">audible-wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/813598-darlene?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/813598-darlene?shelf=anne-mccaffrey">anne-mccaffrey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/813598-darlene?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/813598-darlene?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/813598-darlene?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/813598-darlene?shelf=kindle-books-i-own">kindle-books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/813598-darlene?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/813598-darlene?shelf=text-to-speech-enabled">text-to-speech-enabled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer912153431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12755303573380608996">It is no secret that Anne McCaffrey has been one of my favorite authors of all time. I think it is within this decade that I was in a bookstore in Reno that had some pretty good deals. They told me that they had just received a huge collection of First Edition Anne McCaffrey's books. I nearly passed it up. I've never been rich monetarily. I figured I wouldn't be able to afford it. But being a store that wanted to keep their merchandise moving, they actually quoted me a price for the whole collec</span>
  <span id="freeText12755303573380608996" style="display:none">It is no secret that Anne McCaffrey has been one of my favorite authors of all time. I think it is within this decade that I was in a bookstore in Reno that had some pretty good deals. They told me that they had just received a huge collection of First Edition Anne McCaffrey's books. I nearly passed it up. I've never been rich monetarily. I figured I wouldn't be able to afford it. But being a store that wanted to keep their merchandise moving, they actually quoted me a price for the whole collection that I could afford.<br /><br />But I was working and found that reading "real" or "tree" books hard for my eyes. And I was always tired with fibromyalgia. So the books sat on my shelves.<br /><br />When we moved here the McCaffreys sat in a box until I got a new bookshelf. Now they are out on display so I can't resist. Except reading the old way is slow. So I try to keep my paper bookmark where I am in the Kindle version and read a bit when I can.<br /><br />Luckily, I've been collecting the Kindle versions of Anne's treasures. At least this one has text-to-speech. I kind of hoped for Audible but they don't have this book. It's okay as I can speed up the listen-rate to 2x and get through a book in no time.<br /><br />As much as I looked forward to Acorna, who wouldn't want to read a story about a unicorn girl? I have to admit that as much as I love her writing style, I found this book wasn't so much about the girl as it was about child slavery and the men who found the girl. You never get to see her point of view, even when she grows up. Still, Ms. McCaffrey and Ms. Ball cover the issues well and made a good story. I am already into the next book and I see the plot continues with other people. Acorna is still not showing up personally. Maybe that will change soon.<br /><br />I still liked the book and can't wait to see what happens in the series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12755303573380608996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3485528533" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3485528533" />
    <a title="Flewts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11385091-flewts"><img alt="Flewts" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3485528533?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flewts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flewts" href="/user/show/11385091-flewts">Flewts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3485528533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7762326547909223722">I re-read this book prior to recommending it for my granddaughter to read, and am glad I did. My daughter and I remember the Acorna series with fondness, but we also are aware that Anne McCaffrey had ... liberal views ... and wanted to make sure this book was appropriate for a young child with advanced reading skills.<br/><br/>Acorna is actually NOT the main character in this book. It is very much a science fiction book, with much discussion of the science involved in keeping air pure on a spaceship, and </span>
  <span id="freeText7762326547909223722" style="display:none">I re-read this book prior to recommending it for my granddaughter to read, and am glad I did. My daughter and I remember the Acorna series with fondness, but we also are aware that Anne McCaffrey had ... liberal views ... and wanted to make sure this book was appropriate for a young child with advanced reading skills.<br /><br />Acorna is actually NOT the main character in this book. It is very much a science fiction book, with much discussion of the science involved in keeping air pure on a spaceship, and other similar topics that use very advanced vocabulary. If this part were read with a parent who could explain it all, it would be OK. However....<br /><br />The main characters are the three men who rescued her as a baby. The issues are adult. One of the characters, Rafik, interacts with his uncle, and they indulge in the time-honored Arab skill of elaborate and creative swearing (son of a camel-whore, etc). The creativity is amusing to an adult, and I'd like to think it would go over a child's head, but it includes graphic descriptions of the removal and disposal of certain male equipment and such that make it unsuitable for a young child.<br /><br />Also a main feature of this book is the abuse of children in child labor, not just working in mines, no work no food, no medical care, children don't live to become adults, etc. But very present is the threat (and reality) of bonk-bonk shops, which are exactly what that sounds like. When girl children reach a certain age....<br /><br />So, at some point this would become suitable reading for a teenager, perhaps after reading the rest of the series (going on to preview Acorna's Quest next...), but not for an elementary age child.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7762326547909223722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1745289721" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1745289721" />
    <a title="Douglas Milewski" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18815007-douglas-milewski"><img alt="Douglas Milewski" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477525827p2/18815007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1745289721?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Douglas Milewski" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Douglas Milewski" href="/user/show/18815007-douglas-milewski">Douglas Milewski</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1745289721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer824165642385854462">Oh, the humanity.<br/><br/>Acorna: The Unicorn Girl (1997), by Anne McCaffey and Margaret Ball, fits into a genre that nobody ever asked for: a vaguely humorous novel about a unicorn girl and child enslavement.<br/><br/>What exactly is this novel trying to be? I have no idea, but like the Hindenburg, it sure does crash and burn well.<br/><br/>I struggle to put this novel into sensible words, mostly because the writers failed to create a novel using sensible words.<br/><br/>The setup is that there's a unicorn girl adopted by three spac</span>
  <span id="freeText824165642385854462" style="display:none">Oh, the humanity.<br /><br />Acorna: The Unicorn Girl (1997), by Anne McCaffey and Margaret Ball, fits into a genre that nobody ever asked for: a vaguely humorous novel about a unicorn girl and child enslavement.<br /><br />What exactly is this novel trying to be? I have no idea, but like the Hindenburg, it sure does crash and burn well.<br /><br />I struggle to put this novel into sensible words, mostly because the writers failed to create a novel using sensible words.<br /><br />The setup is that there's a unicorn girl adopted by three space miners. The "uncles" have names, but as far as I can tell, they're interchangeable characters with no separate personalities. Being that they're three of the primary characters, not having a well developed personalities is rather an creative writing deal breaker for me. <br /><br />I skimmed this book rather than read it because the writing utterly failed to grab my attention on all levels. That should have given me a good idea of the story's main arc, right? RIGHT? But only if there's a coherent main arc, which there wasn't.<br /><br />My biggest fault with the story is that it fails on the tone level, varying the tone wildly, and that tone often being at odds with the events that are occurring in the story. Much of it feels like 1960's fluff SF (which is okay), but unfortunately brings much of the pasts's sexism, racism, and other -isms. Put that fluffiness up against child labor, child exploitation, forced sex worker status, and all that, and it all falls apart in a burning ball of hydrogen and superstructure.<br /><br />I cannot recommend this work. I've read it so that you don't have to.</span>
  <a data-text-id="824165642385854462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2849505408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2849505408" />
    <a title="Javin Stanuary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97052399-javin-stanuary"><img alt="Javin Stanuary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563111339p2/97052399.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2849505408?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Javin Stanuary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Javin Stanuary" href="/user/show/97052399-javin-stanuary">Javin Stanuary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2849505408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4196834690752249701">At some point in my teenage years, I started worrying about bills and college and what I wanted to be when I grew up, and stopped reading Anne McCaffrey books. I've recently been collecting her books from local bookshops and catching up on the ones I missed. Of course there's the few odd Pern books, but I also wanted to read some of the other series. I thought this one was going to be silly, so I kept putting it off. I mean, a unicorn girl? But it's addressed in a serious way, though I wish she </span>
  <span id="freeText4196834690752249701" style="display:none">At some point in my teenage years, I started worrying about bills and college and what I wanted to be when I grew up, and stopped reading Anne McCaffrey books. I've recently been collecting her books from local bookshops and catching up on the ones I missed. Of course there's the few odd Pern books, but I also wanted to read some of the other series. I thought this one was going to be silly, so I kept putting it off. I mean, a unicorn girl? But it's addressed in a serious way, though I wish she had emphasized the earth lore aspect a bit more. The characters aren't as well developed as in some of her other books, but I believe this book was written as her health was beginning to decline and she was getting the help of other writers. In my opinion, the books she collaborated on are not as strong as the ones she wrote alone. There's something charming about her writing that's lost when another person has a hand in it. But I've recently read some absolute turds by other authors and coming back to a McCaffrey book was like breathing fresher air. My last book (The Word Exchange - Alena Graedon) was a weeks long, unenjoyable slog. I finished this book in 2 days. I think that's the sign of a book well enjoyed. It's certainly not my favorite, nor her best, but it made me happy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4196834690752249701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3285156653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6919380667186856315">This one wasn't for me. <br/><br/>A toddler, unicorn-girl alien with purifying, healing powers is found and raised by three bachelor asteroid miners. Throw in a world with exploited extreme poverty and enslaved children in need of rescue and it seems like a magical, feel-good combination of fantasy, sci-fi, and social justice. <br/><br/>But those enslaved children? HIDEOUSLY abused and oppressed. Along with just about all (all except Acorna?) of the women in this book. As I was thinking about it, I realized that th</span>
  <span id="freeText6919380667186856315" style="display:none">This one wasn't for me. <br /><br />A toddler, unicorn-girl alien with purifying, healing powers is found and raised by three bachelor asteroid miners. Throw in a world with exploited extreme poverty and enslaved children in need of rescue and it seems like a magical, feel-good combination of fantasy, sci-fi, and social justice. <br /><br />But those enslaved children? HIDEOUSLY abused and oppressed. Along with just about all (all except Acorna?) of the women in this book. As I was thinking about it, I realized that the bulk of my review was basically just going to be a big content warning. Yes, the good folks are trying to defeat the evil folks, but the characterizations are shallow and uneven, with sexual abuse and the throw-away lives of women and children standing in for much of it. Add in cultural insensitivity and stereotypes and the whole book becomes something that I can't really recommend.<br /><br />It's an interesting premise, there are certainly redeeming characters and characteristics, and I did kind of want to keep reading the series to find out more about Acorna's people and what I suspect is going to be an epic tale on a galactic stage. But alas. There are too many other books calling my name to be hanging out with ones I don't trust at this point. Your mileage, as always, may vary.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6919380667186856315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2707311309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17058700054643861848">This is an excellent example of why you should never judge a book by its cover. Like most female authors, the cover is soft and suggests something akin to a fantasy romance novel. Nothing could be further from the truth. This book has space travel, alien unicorns and a protagonist who is more interested in saving enslaved children than romance. <br/>The writing was disjointed and repetitive at times, but the story itself was unpredictable in the best way and quite entertaining.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YlkQWnrXR7Z+G1YJD8U3KKabX+3fg8ve1h4RSUPbSJ99ik4uPGswF6x4eyqknwy1qv7iB6yGr2K63keouBtN2g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

This ancient land of mystery is unique even among fantasy realms, for it is protected by an elite corps—the Heralds. These men and women gifted with extraordinary mind powers are Chosen by, and bonded with, wondrous horse-like beings known as Companions. Brought by their Companions from the length and breadth of Valdemar to Haven, Valdemar\'s capital city, they are trained in a special school, the Collegium, and devote their lives to protecting king and kingdom. Mindspeakers, FarSeers, FarSpeakers, Firestarters, ForeSeers—their individual talents are as varied as their backgrounds. There are even those who can channel the magical nodes in the earth itself to use for their own purposes. Garbed in their uniforms of white leather, they patrol their territory, dispensing justice and keeping the peace. They are emissaries, spies, diplomats, scouts, warriors, judges, and counselors.\n\nWith eighteen novels published, and millions of copies in print, Mercedes Lackey\'s Valdemar series has won the hearts of countless readers. In response to overwhelming demand on the part of her many fans, veteran editors John Helfers and Denise Little now present The Valdemar Companion. With the help and guidance of Mercedes Lackey, Helfers and Little have compiled a reader\'s guide to Mercedes Lackey\'s best-selling world of Valdemar. Included in this comprehensive work is an all-original Mercedes Lackey Valdemar novella, as well as an essay by Lackey about Valdemar, and extensive interviews with the author and her publisher. The lyrics of an all-but-forgotten song seem to point toward an answer from nearly five hundred years in the past, when Kitti Ping and her daughter Wind Blossom bred the first dragons from their smaller cousins, the fire-lizards. No doubt the first colonists possessed the advanced technology to find the cure for which Lorana seeks, but over the centuries, that knowledge has been lost. Or has it? For in the distant past, an aged Wind Blossom worries that the germs that affect the fire-lizards may one day turn on larger prey-and unleash a plague that will destroy the dragons, Pern\'s only defenders against Thread. But as her people struggle to survive, Wind Blossom has neither the time nor the resources to expend on a future that may never arrive-until suddenly sheuncovers evidence that her worst fears will come true. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6443836851563307003">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br/><br/>Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br/><br/>Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High Scho</span>
  <span id="freeText6443836851563307003" style="display:none">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br /><br />Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br /><br />Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High School in Montclair, New Jersey, and graduated cum laude from Radcliffe College, majoring in Slavonic Languages and Literatures.<br /><br />Her working career included Liberty Music Shops and Helena Rubinstein (1947-1952). She married in 1950 and had three children: Alec Anthony, b. 1952, Todd, b.1956, and Georgeanne, b.1959.<br /><br />Anne McCaffrey’s first story was published by Sam Moskowitz in Science Fiction + Magazine and her first novel was published by Ballantine Books in 1967. By the time the three children of her marriage were comfortably in school most of the day, she had already achieved enough success with short stories to devote full time to writing. Her first novel, Restoree, was written as a protest against the absurd and unrealistic portrayals of women in s-f novels in the 50s and early 60s. It is, however, in the handling of broader themes and the worlds of her imagination, particularly the two series The Ship Who Sang and the fourteen novels about the Dragonriders of Pern that Ms. McCaffrey’s talents as a story-teller are best displayed.<br /><br />She died at the age of 85, after suffering a massive stroke on 21 November 2011.<br /><br />Obituaries: <a href="http://www.locusmag.com/News/2011/11/anne-mccaffrey-1926-2011/" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus</a>, <a href="http://www.mediabistro.com/galleycat/anne-mccaffrey-has-died_b42826" rel="nofollow noopener">GalleyCat</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6443836851563307003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

As Acorna and her Linyaari people begin to rebuild<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText901274966613686645\" style=\"display:none\">The Barnes &amp; Noble Review	Acorna\'s Search, the fifth book in Anne McCaffrey\'s Acorna series, takes the saga of the beloved unicorn girl to an all-time high -- or low, depending on how you look at it. As Acorna and her Linyaari people begin to rebuild their home planet (which was practically destroyed by the evil insectoid Khleevi in Acorna\'s World), members of Linyaarian research parties begin to disappear one by one. Soon whole shuttles are just vanishing into thin air. Among the missing is Acorna\'s life mate, Aari. After consulting with the Ancestors, Acorna concludes that she must go deep underneath the planet\'s surface to solve the potentially horrific mystery.\n	The once cool, idyllic world of Vhiliinyar is now like something out of a nightmare. &quot;The whole planet was, for the most part, stifling, with much of its protective ozone layer punctured by volcanic explosions and toxic chemical reactions from its unstable land masses and destroyed seas.&quot; Instead of green meadows filled with beautiful flora and fauna, there are now carnivorous plants, poisonous geysers, bogs and apelike monsters. While trying to escape these hairy, spear-toting beasts, Acorna is forced deep into a cave and stumbles across the opening into an ancient subterranean city. \n	The mysterious history of the uni-horned Linyaari people is steeped in fable, and when Acorna discovers the mythical city of Kubiilikaan, the legendary home of the Hosts, much of what she thought was historically true becomes suspect. As Acorna unravels the mystery with the help of the royal temple cat Roadkill and Mac the android, she finds out Aari isn\'t lost in space, but in time. \n	For those of you who aren\'t familiar with the series, here\'s a quick overview. In the first book in the series, Acorna, we\'re introduced to the lovable orphan after her family\'s spaceship is mysteriously destroyed. She escapes in a space pod and is found by a salvage ship crewed by three humans. The men had never seen anything quite like Acorna before. The Linyaari were a race of humanoids with unicorn characteristics -- a flowing, curling mane and feathery hair from ankle to knee, hooves, three fingers and, of course, a horn protruding from their foreheads. \n	The men, obviously with nowhere to take the orphan, are forced to raise the strange girl themselves. During their months aboard ship, they bond with the lovable kid and she slowly learns their language and culture. But with none of her kind around, and no way to know if any even still exist, Acorna struggles to find her own identity. When the salvage ship finally returns to Federation space, Acorna becomes the center of attention. Rumors spread like wildfire about a unicorn girl with magical powers.\n	Over the course of the next two novels (Acorna\'s Quest and Acorna\'s People), Acorna finds the Linyaari homeworld and becomes reunited with her people. She learns about her race\'s history and culture and also about its enemies, the Khleevi. I have to tell you, the Khleevi are right up there on my Top Ten list of most despicable aliens. They\'re basically oversized cockroaches that travel the galaxy looking for worlds to plunder and life forms to torture.\n	In Acorna\'s World, the fourth installment, Acorna and her people come face-to-face with the Khleevi, except this time they have the Federation\'s help. \n	I recommend this series to fantasy lovers of all ages. McCaffrey and Scarborough (who coauthored the last three books in the series) create an interesting, realistic world without exploitative sex or violence. And, because the main character is a young, strong, good-hearted female, this series would be particularly perfect for young girls interested in fantasy. \n (Paul Goat Allen)<\/span>\n  <a
